Jamison Brereton

91
Soma
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
23 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ4, g─Бyatr─л 5тАУ16, uс╣гс╣Зih 17, triс╣гс╣нubh 18тАУ23
Long and metrically disunified, this hymn no doubt falls into distinct segments, but there is no scholarly agreement about the exact divisions. Some verse groupings are found together in later liturgical texts (e.g., vss. 16тАУ18, which, though in three dif ferent meters, agree in contents), but in other cases there is no external evidence. It is possible that the triс╣гс╣нubh verses at the beginning (vss. 1тАУ4) and those at the end (vss. 19тАУ23) belong together, with the dimeter verses 5тАУ16 (plus 17тАУ18) having been inserted between them. This is suggested by the fact that verse 19 starts with the same sequence as the beginning of verse 4 (y─Б╠Б te dh─Б╠Бm─Бni), and also by the apparent ring between 1a pr├б cikitaс╕е and 23d pr├б cikits─Б.
In any case this hymn shares both the rather simplified rhetoric and the totalizing thematics of GotamaтАЩs hymns to the All Gods. Soma is identified with numerous224 I.91
gods (see, e.g., vss. 3, 5) and is credited with multiple cosmogonic deeds (e.g., vs. 22) and martial powers (e.g., vs. 21). Especially in the g─Бyatr─л verses he is begged for all sorts of aid and comradeship.
Since this is not a Soma Pavam─Бna hymn and is not found in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala, the ritual details that dominate that maс╣Зс╕Нala are essentially absent here. The exception is the aforementioned triad of verses 16тАУ18, each of which contains a form of ─Б╠Б тИЪpy─Б тАЬswell,тАЭ an idiom used of the soaking of the soma stalks in water to make them swell up before their pressing. As this action occurs before the puri
fication process proper, it is hardly mentioned in the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala (twice in fact, once [IX.31.4] in an exact repetition of the present vs. 16 in a hymn attributed to our poet Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa), while it is the most prominent ritual detail in this hymn.

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are thoroughly apprehended by our understanding; you lead us along a straight path; by your guidance, Indra, our righteous fathers obtained wealth among the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, have become conspicuous through our inspired thought. YouтАФlead along the straightest path.
Through your guidance, o drop, our insightful forefathers had their
share in the treasure among the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The multiple possible meanings of the root(s) тИЪcit and the unclear morphological identity of (pr├б) cikitaс╕е make the interpretation of the first p─Бda somewhat difficult. I follow ThiemeтАЩs solution (Plusq.), adopted also by K├╝mmel (176-77), that it is underlyingly a medial injunctive to the perfect stem (that is, an unaugmented pluperfect), patterning with pf. cikit├й, etc. But the underspecification of this posited

*cikita caused it to be re-marked with an active ending (like root presents of the type aduha-t). It should not be a subjunctive, despite its thematic appearance, because of the zero-grade root syllable, and, pace Witzel Got┼Н, it should not be a trans./caus.

reduplicated aorist because of the light reduplicating syllable (expect *c─лkitas) – although I do have to admit that acikitat in VII.80.2 does seem to function like a redupl. aorist. Witzel Got┼Н supply panth─Б╠Бm, from b, as object in a, but this seems unnecessary. On a potential ring made by pr├б cikitaс╕е here and pr├б cikits─Б in the last p─Бda of the hymn (23d), see published introduction. The other question in p─Бda a is whose inspired thought is at issue. I assume that it is ours (that is, the poetsтАЩ), in that the priests and poets create the ritual that makes soma manifest.

Our wise forefathers by thy guidance, Indu, dealt out among the Gods their share of treasure.

рдЕрде рд╕реЛрдорд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рд░реНрде рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are the doer of good by holy acts; you are powerful by your energies, and know all things; you are the showerer (of benefits) by your bounties, and (are great) by your greatness; you, the guide of men, has been well nourished by sacrificial offerings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, become very intent through your intentions; very skillful with your skills, all-knowing.
You are a bull through your bullish powers, your greatness. You became brilliant through your brilliancies, drawing the gaze of men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is structured by a series of etymological figures involving a nom. sg. modifying soma and an instr. pl. specifying his qualities – a: kr├бtubhiс╕е sukr├бtuс╕е, b: d├бkс╣гaiс╕е sud├бkс╣гaс╕е, c: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б vс╣Ыс╣гatv├йbhiс╕е, d: dyumn├йbhir dyumn─л╠Б. It is a not a subtle device, but effective. On the first hemistich see further ad vs. 14.

Griffith

Thou by thine insight art most wise, O Soma, strong by thine energies and all possessing,
Mighty art thou by all thy powers and greatness, by glories art thou glorious, guide of mortals.

Geldner

Du, Soma, bist an Einsicht wohleinsichtig, an Verstand wohlverst├дndig, du der Allwissende. Du bist ein Bulle an Bullenst├дrke, an Gr├╢├Яe; du mit dem Herrenauge wardst glanzreich an Glanz.

Grassmann

Durch Einsicht bist du einsichtsvoll, o Soma, durch Kr├дfte kr├дftig, du der Allbesitzer; Ein Stier bist du durch Stiereskraft und Gr├╢sse, durch Reichthum wurdest reich du M├дnnerschauer.

Elizarenkova

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYour acts are (like those) of the royal Varuс╣Зa; your glory, Soma, is great and profound; you are the purifier (of all), like the beloved Mitra; you are the augmenter of all, like Aryaman.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

R─Бj├▒o varuс╣Зasya: y─Бg─Бrtham ─Бhс╣Ыtaс╕е kс╣Ыto vastreс╣З─Бvс╣Ыtaс╕е soma varuс╣Зaс╕е: varuс╣Зa means that which is enclosed in a cloth, or the Soma which has been purchased for a sacrifice. soma asm─Бkam br─Бhmaс╣З─Бn─Бm r─Бj─Б, soma is the king of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.8.10.2); somaraj─Бno br─Бhmaс╣Зaс╕е, the br─Бhmaс╣Зas have soma for king

Jamison Brereton

The commandments of King Varuс╣Зa are yours; lofty and deep is your domain, o Soma.
You are blazing pure, like dear Mitra. You are besought for skill like Aryaman, o Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Soma is here identified with the three principal ─Аdityas. This vs. is identical to IX.88.8, though the two published translation differ in p─Бda b. I would now alter the tr. here to тАЬyours is his lofty, deep domain, o Soma.тАЭ See disc. ad IX.88.8.

The (pseudo-)gerundive dakс╣г─Б╠Бyya- has attracted a number of different renderings – in this passage alone, Geldner тАЬzu Gunst geneigt,тАЭ Renou тАЬquтАЩon doit-servirefficacement,тАЭ Witzel Got┼Н тАЬals Zufriedenzustellender.тАЭ I prefer to tie it more closely with d├бkс╣гa- тАШskillтАЩ, as тАЬwhose skill is to be sought,тАЭ despite the awkwardness of the English gloss. In this passage Soma was just credited with skill (2b) and will later dispense it (7c; cf. also 14c), and in both I.129.2 and VII.97.8 the ability of Indra and Bс╣Ыhaspati to bring about good things is emphasized. JPB in VII.1.2 prefers тАЬto be skillfully tended,тАЭ quite close to RenouтАЩs rendering above. This latter tr. would work for Agni (II.4.3, VII.1.2), who requires ritual tending, but less well for Indra, Bс╣Ыhaspati, and (here) Aryaman.

Griffith

Thine are King Varuna’s eternal statutes, lofty and deep, O Soma, is thy glory.
All-pure art thou like Mitra the beloved, adorable, like Aryaman, O Soma.

Geldner

Deine Gebote sind wie die des K├╢nigs Varuna; hoch und tief ist dein Wesen, o Soma. Du bist lauter wie der liebe Mitra; wie Aryaman bist du zu Gunst geneigt, o Soma.

Grassmann

Dein sind des K├╢nigs Varuna Gesetze, hoch ist und tief, o Soma, deine St├дtte, Du strahltest hell so wie der liebe Mitra, du Soma bist wie Arjaman zu ehren,

Elizarenkova

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬEndowed with all the glories (that are displayed) by you in heaven, on earth, in the mountains, in the plural nts, in the waters, do you, illustrious Soma, well-disposed towards us, and devoid of anger, accept our oblations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Illustrious Soma = royal (r─Бjan) soma

Jamison Brereton

Your domains that are in heaven, that are on the earth, that are in the mountains, in the plants, in the watersтАФ
with all those, being well-disposed and not angry, King Soma, accept our oblations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The perennially difficult dh─Б╠Бman-, found also in 3b, is a bit difficult to interpret here as well. In both 3b and 4ab, the dh─Б╠Бman- appear to be concrete and locatable in space, for which the tr. тАШdomain(s)тАЩ fits well (cf. also Witzel Got┼Н тАЬSt├дttenтАЭ). But then in cd Soma is urged to accept our oblations with them, which seems difficult to do with a place and edges closer to GeldnerтАЩs тАЬFormen,тАЭ a nebulous and all-purpose rendering that I try to avoid with this word. RenouтАЩs тАЬstructuresтАЭ doesnтАЩt help either. I must assume that тАЬaccept with all your (domains)тАЭ is a compressed way of saying тАЬwherever you are, accept.тАЭ The same problem is found, to some extent, in vs. 19.

Griffith

With all thy glories on the earth, in heaven, on mountains, in the plants, and in the waters,–
With all of these, well-pleased and not in anger, accept, O royal Soma, our oblations.

Geldner

Deine Formen im Himmel, auf Erden, die auf den Bergen, in den Pflanzen, im Wasser sind, mit allen diesen nimm wohlgesinnt, nicht ├╝belnehmend, unsere Opfer an, o K├╢nig Soma!

Grassmann

In alle St├дtten, die du hast im Himmel, auf Erden und in Bergen, Kr├дutern, Wassern, In die nimm huldvoll auf, o K├╢nig Soma, und ohne Z├╝rnen unsre Opfertr├дnke.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, are the protector, the soverign of the pious, or even the slayer of Vс╣Ыtra; you are holy sacrifice..тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Satpatis tvam r─Бj─Б uta: sat may also mean br─Бhmaс╣Зa, hence: the protector, or lord (pati), or the king (r─Бj─Б of the br─Бhmaс╣Зas); you are holy sacrifice: Soma is identified with the sacrifice, from the essential part it performs in it: tadr┼лpo bhavanti s─Бdhyatv─Бd yaj├▒─Бn─Бm

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, fond of praise, the lord of plural nts, are life to us; if you will, we shall not die.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Somo v─Б oс╣гadh─лn─Бm r─Бj─Б (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 6.1.9.1)

Jamison Brereton

And if you will wish us to live, Soma, we will not die.
(You are) the lord of the forest to whom praise is dear.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A good example of subordinating ca.

On the use of v├бnasp├бti- тАШlord of the forestтАЩ for soma, see comm. ad IX.12.7.

This usage is found only here and in IX.12.7. Because our phrase priy├бstotro v├бnasp├бtiс╕е is almost identical to IX.12.7 n├нtyastotro v├бnasp├бtiс╕е, I am now inclined to translate the bahuvr. тАШwho has praise as his ownтАЩ, not тАШto whom praise is dearтАЩ.

Griffith

And, Soma, let it be thy wish that we may live and may not die:
Praise-loving Lord of plants art thou.

Geldner

So du, Soma, willst, da├Я wir leben, so sterben wir nicht. Du bist der preisliebende Baumf├╝rst.

Grassmann

Wenn du uns, Soma, leben heisst, so fall’n wir nicht dem Tod anheim, O Waldesf├╝rst, dem Lob gef├дllt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou bestow, Soma, upon him who worships, you, whether old or young, wealth, what he may enjoy and live.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, (establish) good fortune for the great man, you, for the youth who pursues the truth;
you establish skill for living.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner and Renou both point out, the dat. y┼л╠Бne тАШyouthтАЩ in b suggests that the parallel mah├й in a refers specifically to an adult.

To him who keeps the law, both old and young, thou givest happiness,
And energy that he may live.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSoma, be our protector with those assistances which are sources of happiness to the donor (of oblations).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma, your forms of help that are joy itself for the pious man,
with those become our helper.

Griffith

With those delightful aids which thou hast, Soma, for the worshipper,–
Even with those protect thou us.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAccepting this our sacrifice, and this our praise, approach, Soma, and be to us as the augmenter of our rite.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This sacrifice hereтАФhaving delighted in this speech, come near to it. Soma, be (ready) to strengthen us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the pf. part. jujuс╣г─Бс╣З├бс╕е as expressing an action anterior to that of the main verb, impv. up─Б╠Бgahi. If this is correct, the verse is constructed chiastically, with im├бс╣Г yaj├▒├бm construed with up─Б╠Бgahi, while the call that precedes SomaтАЩs arrival at the sacrifice is nested in between (id├бс╣Г v├бco, jujuс╣г─Бn├бс╕е).

Griffith

Accepting this our sacrifice and this our praise, O Soma, come,
And be thou nigh to prosper us.

Geldner

An diesem Opfer, an dieser Rede dich erfreuend komm herbei! Sei du, Soma, uns zum Gedeihen!

Grassmann

Lass dieses Opfer, dieses Lied gefallen dir und komm herbei, O Soma, du sei uns zum Heil.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSoma, dwell happy in our hearts, like cattle in fresh pastures, like men in their own abodes.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma, take pleasure in our heart, as cows do in pastures,
as a young man in his prime does in his own home.

Griffith

Soma, be happy in our heart, as milch-kine in the grassy meads,
As a young man in his own house.

Geldner

Soma! Verweile gern in unserem Herzen wie die K├╝he auf der Weide, wie ein junger Mann im eigenen Heim!

Grassmann

Erquick an unserm Herzen dich, o Soma, wie die Kuh am Gras, Und wie der Mann am eignen Haus.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe experienced sage commends the mortal who, through affection, divine Soma, praises you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Soma, the mortal who will take pleasure in your comradeship, o god, him does skill accompany, him does the sage poet.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although it is tempting to take d├бkс╣гa- as adjectival here (so Geldner, Witzel Got┼Н), I am somewhat dubious that this stem can be an adjective, and in any case the emphasis on the skill associated with Soma in this hymn (vss. 2b, 3d, 7c) suggests a nominal reading here. Although the pairing of an abstract quality (skill) with an animate being (poet) might seem awkward, I see it as a variant reprise of 2ab, where kr├бtu- (тАШintentionтАЩ) and d├бkс╣гa- were paired; as discussed ad I.2.7-9, kr├бtu- and d├бkс╣гa- are two of the three qualities required to bring an action about and are regularly associated. Here kav├н- stands in for kr├бtu-. This substitution is enabled by the syntagm тАЬthe poetтАЩs kr├бtu-, as in the cmpd. kav├н-kratu-. (RenouтАЩs interpr. is similar; see his n.)

Griffith

O Soma, God, the mortal man who in thy friendship hath delight,
Him doth the mighty Sage befriend.

Geldner

Welcher Sterbliche, o Gott Soma, in deiner Gesellschaft gern verweilt, dem steht der wirksame Seher zur Seite.

Grassmann

Welch Sterblicher, o Gott, sich freut, o Soma, deiner Br├╝derschaft, Dem ist der starke Seher hold.

English translation:

тАЬProtect us, Soma, from calumny, preserve us from sin; plural ased with our service, be our friend.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Uruс╣гyat─л rakс╣гakarm─Б (Nirukta 5.23)

Jamison Brereton

Make a broad space for us against imprecation; Soma, protect us from narrow straits.
Be a comrade well disposed to us.

Griffith

Save us from slanderous reproach, keep us., O Soma, from distress:
Be unto us a gracious Friend.

English translation:

тАЬExulting Soma, increase with all twining plural nts; be to us a friend; well supplied with food, we may prosper.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъravaс╕е ityann─Бma (Nirukta 10.3)

Jamison Brereton

Swell up, most exhilarating Soma, with all your shoots.
Become our comrade of best fame, to strengthen us.

Griffith

Wax, O most gladdening Soma, great through all thy rays of light, and be
A Friend of most illustrious fame to prosper us.

Geldner

Quill auf, berauschender Soma, mit allen Stengeln; sei du der gern erh├╢rende Freund uns zum Gedeihen!

Grassmann

Schwill an von Saft, berauschendster, in allen Fasern, Soma du, Sei uns der hochber├╝hmteste, ein Freund zum Heil.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton

Let your milk-drinks come together and together your prizes, together the bullish powers of you who vanquish hostility.
Swelling up for the immortal, Soma, establish your own highest
measures of fame in heaven.

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhichever of your glories (men) worship with oblations, may our sacrifice be invested with them all; come to our mansions, Soma, who are the bestower of wealth, the transporter (over difficulties); attended by valiant heroes, the non-destroyer of progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Those domains of yours that they sacrifice to with oblation, let all these of yours be encompassing the sacrifice.
Fattening the livestock, furthering (us), bringing good heroes, not
smiting heroes, o Soma, advance to our doorways.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here again, as in vs. 4, the dh─Б╠Бm─Бni of Soma are recipients of the oblation; GeldnerтАЩs Formen again works more smoothly, but I still consider these to be the locales listed in 4ab, each of which can be a site of sacrifice.

Note the disharmony in number between the neut. pl. subj. (t─Б╠Бvi┼Ыv─Б) and the sg. pred. nom. (paribh┼л╠Бс╕е) and verb (astu). This could be an example of the inherited construction of neuter pl. with a singular verb, but I think itтАЩs more likely just a constructio ad sensum, with тАЬall theseтАЭ summarizing the plural subjects of the rel. cl.

as if in a mass. English тАЬall thisтАЭ can be similarly used, after a listing of discrete entities. The Sanskrit has just been more punctilious about maintaining number agreement.

Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н all supply тАШlifetimeтАЩ as the implicit object of prat├бraс╣Зaс╕е, rather than my тАШusтАЩ; they are most likely correct, given how common the idiom ─Б╠Бyus- pr├б тИЪtс╣Э is. I might change the published translation to тАЬlengthening (our lifetime).тАЭ

Such of thy glories as with poured oblations men honour, may they all invest our worship.
Wealth-giver, furtherer with troops of heroes, sparing the brave, come, Soma, to our houses.

рдпрдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рджрджрд╛рд╢рддреН рд╕реЛрдорд╛рдп рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рдиреНрдпрдиреНрдирд╛рдирд┐ рджрджреНрдпрд╛рддреН рддрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рд╕реЛрдордГ рдзреЗрдиреБрдВ рд╕рд╡рддреНрд╕рд╛рдВ рджреЛрдЧреНрдзреНрд░реАрдВ рдЧрд╛рдВ рджрджрд╛рддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЖрд╢реБ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рдЧрд╛рдорд┐рдирдореН рдЕрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдВ рджрджрд╛рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рд╡реАрд░рдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╛рдп рджрджрд╛рддрд┐ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢рдВ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдореН ред рдХрд░реНрдордгреНрдпрдВ рд▓реМрдХрд┐рдХрдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рдХреБрд╢рд▓рдВ рд╕рджрдиреНрдпрдореН ред рд╕рджрдирдВ рдЧреГрд╣рдореН ред рддрджрд░реНрд╣рдореН ред рдЧреНрд░реГрд╣рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдХреБрд╢рд▓рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╡рд┐рджрдереНрдпрдореН ред рд╡рд┐рджрдиреНрддреНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджрдерд╛рдГ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ ред рддрджрд░реНрд╣рдореН ред рджрд░реНрд╢рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдорд╛рд╕рд╛рджрд┐рдпрд╛рдЧрд╛рдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рдирдкрд░рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕рднреЗрдпрдВ рд╕рднрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдореН ред рд╕рдХрд▓рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рднрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдкрд┐рддреГрд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрдВ рдкрд┐рддрд╛ рд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрддреЗ рдпреЗрди рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗрдг рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдореН рее рдХрд░реНрдордгреНрдпрдореН ред рдХрд░реНрдорд╕реБ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгреНрдпрдГ ред

’ рддрддреНрд░ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдГ ‘( рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рек. рек. репрео) рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрддреН ред ’ рдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рдХрд░реНрдордгреЛрдГ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред ’ рддрд┐рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░рд┐рддрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рд┐рддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдПрд╡рдореБрддреНрддрд░рддреНрд░рд╛рдкрд┐ рдпрддреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рд╕рднреЗрдпрдореН ред ’ рдврд╢реНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ ( рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рек. рек. резрежрем) рдЗрддрд┐ рддрддреНрд░ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдГ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рдбрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рджрджрд╛рд╢рддреН ред ’ рджрд╛рд╢реГ рджрд╛рдиреЗ ’ ред рд▓реЗрдЯрд┐ рдЕрдбрд╛рдЧрдордГ ред ’ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рдкрдГ рд╢реНрд▓реБрдГ ред ред ред ред реиреи ред ред

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬTo him who present (offerings), Soma gives a cow, a swift horse, and a son who is able in affairs, skilful in domestic concerns, assiduous in worship, eminent in society, and who is an honour to his father.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma gives a milk-cow, Soma a swift steed, Soma a hero fit for actionтАФ one fit for the residence, for the rite, for the assembly, one who brings fame to the forefathersтАФ(gives these to the man) who will do ritual service to him.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) takes the final phrase of d y├│ d├бd─Б┼Ыad asmai as expressing the indirect object with dad─Бti in b (тАЬgives [to him,] who тАжтАЭ), rather than as a qualification of v─лr├бm (or even of pitс╣Ы-, as Renou almost seems to). I think this is correct, but it is mildly disturbing that there is no overt expression of the datival recipient in the main clause; we would expect t├бsmai (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 20d). It may have been gapped because of the asmai in the rel. clause. Note that asmai cannot be a part of the main clause and refer to the indirect object, the man who does pious service, because it is unaccented; it must be part of the rel. cl. and refer to Soma.

Griffith

To him who worships Soma gives the milch-cow, a fleet steed and a man of active knowledge,
Skilled in home duties, meet for holy synod, for council meet, a glory to his father.

Geldner

Soma schenkt dem, der ihm opfert, eine Milchkuh, Soma ein rasches Streitro├Я, Soma einen werkt├╝chtigen Sohn, der im Haus, im Rat der Weisen, in der Versammlung t├╝chtig ist, der dem Vater Ruhm bringt.

Grassmann

Die Kuh schenkt Soma, schnelle Rosse Soma, er schenkt den Sohn, der t├╝chtig ist im Werke, Im Hause t├╝chtig, in dem Fest, im Rathe, den V├дtern ruhmvoll, der dem Soma huldigt.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe rejoice, Soma, contemplating you, invincible in battle, triumphant amongst hosts, the granter of heaven, the giver of rain, the preserver of strength, born amidst sacrifices, occupying a brilliant dwelling, renowned and victorious.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Invincible in combats, in battles a deliverer, winning the sun, winning the waters, herdsman of the community,
born at raids, granting good dwelling and good fame, conqueringтАФyou would we celebrate, o Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse plays a minor syntactic trick. It consists of a string of acc. sg.

masc. qualifiers; since the previous vs. also consists largely of an acc. sg. masc. NP headed by v─лr├бm, the audience would be likely to assume that the new series of grammatically matching adjectives are also qualifiers of v─лr├бm, esp. since this type of syntactic dependence between verses is not uncommon in the RV. It is only when we arrive at the middle of the final p─Бda that we encounter tv─Б╠Бm and discover that the accusatives of this verse refer to Soma, not to the hero he gives us in 22.

Geldner accounts for the curious hapax bhareс╣гu-j─Б╠Б- тАШborn at raidsтАЩ by the fact that soma is especially offered before battle. This is probably correct, though the semantics could be tighter. Scarlatta essentially accepts this explanation and cites III.51.8 (of soma) j─Бt├бm тАж mah├й bh├бr─Бya, though he explores some other possibilities as well.

Griffith

Invincible in fight, saver in battles, guard of our camp, winner of light and water,
Born amid hymns, well-housed, exceeding famous, victor, in thee will we rejoice, O Soma.

Geldner

Wir m├╢chten dir, Soma, zujubeln als dem Sieger, der in den K├дmpfen unbezwungen, in den Schlachten heraushilft, der das Himmelslicht gewinnt, das Wasser gewinnt, dem Hirten der Opferpartei, dem Kampfgeborenen, der gute Wohnsitze, guten Ruhm erwirbt.

Grassmann

Dich der du beistehst unbesiegt in Schlachten, verschaffend Glanz und Wasser, Wohnung schirmend, Zum Kampf geboren, sch├╢n an Ruhm und Wohnsitz, dich Sieger, Soma, wollen wir begr├╝ssen.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рд╕реЛрдо рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЗрдорд╛рдГ рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдкрдГ рддрд╛рд╕рд╛рдореЛрдзреАрдирд╛рдВ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрднреВрддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрдпреБрджрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЧрд╛: рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкрд╢реВрдиреБрджрдкрд╛рджрдпрдГ ред рдЙрд░реБ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдореН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЖ рддрддрдиреНрде рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдирдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рдпрддреН рддрдордГ рдирд┐рд░реЛрдзрдХрдордиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рддрджрдкрд┐ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рдЖрддреНрдореАрдпреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди рд╡рд┐ рд╡рд╡рд░реНрде рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрддрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рд╡рд┐рдирд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ рее рддрддрдиреНрде ред рддрдиреБ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░реЗ ред рд╡рд╡рд░реНрде ред рд╡реГрдЮреН рд╡рд░рдгреЗ ред рдЙрднрдпрддреНрд░ рд▓рд┐рдЯрд╕реНрдерд▓рд┐ тАв рдмрднреВрдерд╛ рддрддрдиреНрде рдЬрдЧреГрднреНрдо рд╡рд╡рд░реНрдереЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рдЧрдореЗ ’ ( рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рен. реи. ремрек ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддреНрдпрддреЗ рее

рд╣реЗ рд╕реЛрдо рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЗрдорд╛ рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ рдЙрддреНрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдордкреЛ рдЬрд▓рд╛рдиреНрдпрдЬрдирдпрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЧрд╛рдГ рдЧрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдкрд╢реВрдирдЬрдирдпрдГ ред
рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдореБрд░реБ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдордиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдВ рдЖрддрддрдиреНрде рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рддрдореЛрд╜рдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рд╡рд╡рд░реНрде рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕рд┐ рее

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou, Soma, have genitive rated all these herbs, the water and the kine; you have spread out the spacious firmament; you have scattered darkness with light.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You, Soma, begot all these plants here; you the waters, you the cows. You have stretched across the wide midspace; you have uncovered the darkness with your light.

Griffith

These herbs, these milch-kine, and these running waters, all these, O Soma, thou hast generated.
The spacious firmament hast thou expanded, and with the light thou hast dispelled the darkness.

Geldner

Du hast alle diese Pflanzen, o Soma, du die Gew├дsser, du die K├╝he hervorgebracht. Du hast den weiten Luftraum ausgespannt; du hast mit dem Lichte das Dunkel aufgedeckt.

Grassmann

Du hast, o Soma, alle diese Pflanzen, die Rinder du erzeugt und die Gew├дsser, Hast ausgespannt den weiten Raum der L├╝fte, und hast enth├╝llt die Finsterniss durch Lichtglanz.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рд╕реЛрдо) рд╕рдорд╕реНрдд рдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЖрд░реЛрдЧреНрдпрдкрди рдФрд░ рдмрд▓ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ ! рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдХрд╛рд░рдг (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЖрдк (рдЗрдорд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕рдорд╕реНрдд (рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ) рд░реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реЛ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЖрдк (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЖрдк (рдЧрд╛рдГ) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдФрд░ рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд┐рдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реЛ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЖрдк (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдард╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢ рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореН) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдХреЛ (рдЙрд░реБ) рдмрд╣реБрдд (рдЖ) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреА рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рддрддрдиреНрде) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реЛ рдФрд░ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЖрдк рдЙрдХреНрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рддрдордГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛, рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд┐рдд рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐ рд╡рд╡рд░реНрде) рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░ рдирд╣реАрдВ рдХрд░рддреЗ, рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдЖрдк рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рд╣реИрдВ рее реиреи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдиреЗ рдирд╛рдирд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреА рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдмрдирд╛рдИ рд╣реИ, рд╡рд╣реА рд╕рдм рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрджреЗрд╡ рд╣реИрдВ рее реиреи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╕реЛрдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдпрддрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪреЗрдорд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рдУрд╖рдзреАрд░рдЬрдирдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдордкрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЧрд╛рд╢реНрдЪрд╛рдЬрдирдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛рд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореБрд░реНрд╡рд╛рддрддрдиреНрде рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рддрдореЛ рд╡рд┐ рд╡рд╡рд░реНрде рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрднрд╡рд╛рдирд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрдГ рд╕реЗрд╡реНрдпрдГ рее реиреи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЬрдЧрджреАрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ (рдЗрдорд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖реАрднреВрддрд╛рдГ (рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд░реЛрдЧрдирд╛рд╢рд┐рдХрд╛рдГ рд╕реЛрдорд╛рджреНрдпреЛрд╖рдзреАрдГ (рд╕реЛрдо) рд╕реЛрдореНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди рдЖрд░реЛрдЧреНрдпрдмрд▓рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдХ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдЕрдЦрд┐рд▓рд╛рдГ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдмрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ рд╡рд╛ (рдЕрдЬрдирдпрдГ) рдЬрдирдпрд╕рд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд▓рдбрд░реНрдереЗ рд▓рдЩреНред (рддреНрд╡рдореН) рдЕрдпрдВ рд╡рд╛ (рдЧрд╛рдГ) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╛рдиреНрд╡рд╛ (рддреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЖ) (рддрддрдиреНрде) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрдгреЛрд╖рд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдмрднреВрдерд╛рддрддрдиреНрдердЬрдЧреГрднреНрдорд╡рд╡рд░реНрдереЗрддрд┐ рдирд┐рдЧрдореЗред рдЕреж ренред реиред ремрекред рдЕрдиреЗрди рд╕реВрддреНрд░реЗрдгрд╛рддрддрдиреНрде, рд╡рд╡рд░реНрдереЗрддреНрдпреЗрддреМ рдирд┐рдкрд╛рддреНрдпреЗрддреЗред (рдЙрд░реБ) рдмрд╣реБ (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореН) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢рдореН (рддреНрд╡рдореН) (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрди рд╢реАрддрд▓реЗрди рддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рд╣рд┐) рд╡рд┐рдЧрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рддрдордГ) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрджреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд░рдХрдВ рд╡рд╛рд╜рдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдореН (рд╡рд╡рд░реНрде) рд╡реГрдгреЛрд╖рд┐ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд▓рд┐рдЯреН рее реиреи рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDivine and potent Soma, bestow upon us, with your brilliant mind, a portion of wealth; may no (adversary) annoy you; you are supreme over the valour of (any) two (mutual) opponents; defend us (from our enemies) in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Allusions to Soma, the product of the earth and Soma, the moon

Jamison Brereton

With your god(like) mind, god Soma, battle for a share of wealth for us, mighty one.
DonтАЩt let it hold out on you. You are master of heroism. On behalf of both (men and gods? / singers and patrons?) be on the lookout in the quest for cattle.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the phrase dev├йna тАж m├бnas─Б we again confront a noun (dev├б-) that seems to be used adjectivally (see vs. 14 above). I have half given in to this temptation, with тАЬgod(like).тАЭ The verb ─Б╠Бtanat in c poses some difficulties in interpretation. Surprisingly, none of the standard tr. who discuss the phrase notes that the same lexeme (─Б╠БтИЪtan) appears in the previous verse (22c) in the same metrical position and in a common, almost clich├йd╠Б usage. I think that ─Б╠Бtanat here is a slangy expression, deliberately constrasting with the high-style cosmic-description usage of ─Б╠Бtatantha in 22. I take the subject to be the wealth (or share of wealth) of b, rather than the m├бnas- of a, as Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take it, nor would I following Renou in taking it as an impersonal construction.

It is not entirely clear who the тАЬbothтАЭ are in d: Geldner singers and patrons, Renou men and gods.

Geldner supplies тАШpathтАЩ with pr├б cikits─Б (тАЬsei тАж der PfadfinderтАЭ) on the basis of IV.47.20. This is possible, and might even be supported by the panth─Б╠Бm in vs. 1, since pr├б cikits─Б seems to form a slight ring with pr├б cikitaс╕е in 1a. However, the verb does not need an object, in my opinion; the desiderative here can express a general intention to be alertly perceptive.

Griffith

Do thou, God Soma, with thy Godlike spirit, victorious, win for us a share of riches.
Let none prevent thee: thou art Lord of valour. Provide for both sides in the fray for booty.

Geldner

Mit deinem g├╢ttlichen Geist, o Soma, erk├дmpfe uns den Anteil am Reichtum, du Gewaltiger! Nicht soll er dich davon abhalten; du besitzest die Kraft. Sei du f├╝r beide Teile beim Rindererwerb der Pfadfinder!

Grassmann

Mit G├╢ttersinn, Gott Soma, kraftbegabter, erk├дmpf uns unsern Antheil an dem Reichthum, Nichts hemme dich; denn Heldenkraft ist dein ja, im Kampf zeig h├╝lfreich F├╝rsten dich und S├дngern.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд╣ рдХреИрд╕рд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рд╕рд╣рд╕рд╛рд╡рдиреН) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН (рджреЗрд╡) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди (рд╕реЛрдо) рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдФрд░ рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдХреЗ рдЕрдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ ! рдЖрдк (рджреЗрд╡реЗрди) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрдпреБрдХреНрдд (рдордирд╕рд╛) рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрдзрди рдХреЗ рд▓рд╛рдн рдХреЛ (рдЕрднрд┐) рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдореНрдореБрдЦ (рдпреБрдзреНрдп) рдпреБрджреНрдз рдХреАрдЬрд┐рдпреЗ рдЬреЛ рдЖрдк (рдирдГ) рд╣рдорд╛рд░реЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдзрди рдХреЗ (рднрд╛рдЧрдореН) рднрд╛рдЧ рдХреЗ (рдИрд╢рд┐рд╖реЗ) рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рд╣реЛ рдЙрд╕ (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреБрдЭрдХреЛ (рдЧрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМ) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдп рдФрд░ рднреВрдорд┐ рдХреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЛрдВ рдХреА рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реБ (рдорд╛ рддрдирддреН) рдкреАрдбрд╝рд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рди рдХрд░реЗрдВред рдЖрдк (рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдХреЛ (рдЙрднрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ) рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдФрд░ рдкрд░рд╛рдпреЗ рдпреЛрджреНрдзрд╛рдУрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдорд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╕) рд╕рдВрд╢рдпрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдордд рд╣реЛ рее реирей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рдкрд░рдо рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рдФрд░ рдУрд╖рдзрд┐рдЧрдг рдХрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рдФрд░ рдпреБрджреНрдз рдореЗрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐ рдХрд░ рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдЕрдкрдиреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдХреЛ рдЬреЛрдбрд╝ рдФрд░ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреА рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдХрд╛ рдкрд░рд╛рдЬрдп рдХрд░ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдп рдХреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдВ рее реирей реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдкрдврд╝рдиреЗ-рдкрдврд╝рд╛рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЗ рдкрдврд╝рдиреЗ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рдХреА рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рд╕реЛрдо) рд╢рдмреНрдж рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рдХрдерди рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ репрез рдЗрдХреНрдХрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ реирей рддреЗрдИрд╕ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╕рд╣рд╕рд╛рд╡рдиреН рджреЗрд╡ рд╕реЛрдо рддреНрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡реЗрди рдордирд╕рд╛ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд░рд╛рдпреЛрд╜рднрд┐рдпреБрдзреНрдп рдпрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН рд░рд╛рдпреЛ рднрд╛рдЧрдореАрд╢рд┐рд╖реЗ рддрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЧрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд░реНрдорд╛ рддрдирддреН рдХреНрд▓реЗрд╢рдпреБрдХреНрддрдВ рдХреНрд▓реЗрд╢рдкреНрд░рджрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдорд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдпреЛрднрдпреЗрднреНрдпреЛ рдорд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╕ рее реирей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджреЗрд╡реЗрди) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрдиреЗрди (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдордирд╕рд╛) рд╢рд┐рд▓реНрдкрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░реЗрдг (рджреЗрд╡) рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгрд╕рдореНрдкрдиреНрди (рд╕реЛрдо) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╕реНрдп (рднрд╛рдЧрдореН) рднрдЬрдиреАрдпрдордВрд╢рдореН (рд╕рд╣рд╕рд╛рд╡рдиреН) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНред рд╕рд╣рд╕реЗрддреНрдпрд╡реНрдпрдпрдореНред рднреВрдорд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдорддреБрдкреН рдЪред (рдЕрднрд┐) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗ (рдпреБрдзреНрдп) рдпреБрдзреНрдпрд╕реНрд╡ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдореИрдкрджрдореНред (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рддреНрд╡рд╛) (рддрдирддреН) рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдпреЗрддреН (рдИрд╢рд┐рд╖реЗ) (рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп) рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдорд╕реНрдп (рдЙрднрдпреЗрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реЛрдорд╛рджреНрдпреЛрд╖рдзрд┐рдЧрдгреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднреНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ (рдкреНрд░) (рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╕) (рдЧрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреМ) рдЧрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рдирд╛рдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдБрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рее реирей рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрдГ рдкрд░рдореЛрддреНрддрдорд╕реНрдп рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрдпреМрд╖рдзрд┐рдЧрдгрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдпреБрджреНрдзрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрдпреЛрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬреНрдп рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд╛рдЬрдпреНрдп рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрд┐рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпреИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддрд┐ рее реирей реердЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдзреНрдпреЗрддреНрд░рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрдпрдирд╛рджрд┐рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рдЪ рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдХрд╕реНрдп рд╕реЛрдорд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдпреЛрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН рее рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрдирд╡рддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ репрез рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ реирей рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рдЕрддреНрдпрдВрдд рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖ рд╡ рдФрд╖рдзреАрдВрдЪрд╛ рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдп рдШреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛ рд╡ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╛рдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддреА рдареЗрд╡реВрди рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рд╛рдиреЗ рдЖрдкрд▓реА рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдЬрдорд╡рд╛рд╡реА рдЖрдгрд┐ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реЗрдиреЗрдЪрд╛ рдкрд░рд╛рднрд╡ рдХрд░реВрди рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреА рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдЪреЗ рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее реирей рее
